### International sporting events {#International_sporting_events}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: International sporting events")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0._Minsk-Arena_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0._Minsk-Arena_-_panoramio_%281%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA-%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0._Minsk-Arena_-_panoramio_(1).jpg) [Minsk Arena](/wiki/Minsk-Arena "Minsk-Arena")

In 2013, Minsk hosted the European Junior Rowing Championships at the Republican Center of Olympic Training for Rowing And Canoeing to the north-west of the city.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-71)^{#cite_ref-71}

Minsk hosted the [2014 IIHF World Championship](/wiki/2014_IIHF_World_Championship "2014 IIHF World Championship") at the [Minsk Arena](/wiki/Arena "Arena").

In January 2016, the [2016 European Speed Skating Championships](/wiki/2016_European_Speed_Skating_Championships "2016 European Speed Skating Championships") were held in the [Minsk Arena](/wiki/Minsk_Arena "Minsk Arena") -- the only indoor speed skating rink in Belarus.

Minsk hosted the [2019 European Games](/wiki/2019_European_Games "2019 European Games") in June.^[\[72\]](#cite_note-72)^{#cite_ref-72}

The [2019 European Figure Skating Championships](/wiki/2019_European_Figure_Skating_Championships "2019 European Figure Skating Championships") were held in the [Minsk Arena](/wiki/Minsk_Arena "Minsk Arena") from 21 to 27 January.  

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  

### Local transport {#Local_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Local transport")\]

Minsk has an extensive public transport system.^[\[73\]](#cite_note-73)^ Passengers are served by 8 tramway lines, over 70 [trolleybus lines](/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Minsk "Trolleybuses in Minsk"), 3 subway lines and over 100 bus lines. Trams were the first public transport used in Minsk (since 1892 -- the horse-tram, and since 1929 -- the electric tram). Public buses have been used in Minsk since 1924, and trolleybuses since 1952.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-74)^^[\[75\]](#cite_note-75)^{#cite_ref-75}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/AKSM_E321_electrobus_in_Minsk_4.jpg/220px-AKSM_E321_electrobus_in_Minsk_4.jpg)](/wiki/File:AKSM_E321_electrobus_in_Minsk_4.jpg) Electrobus AKSM E321 in Minsk

All public transport is operated by Minsktrans, a government-owned and -funded transport [not-for-profit](/wiki/Non-profit_organisation "Non-profit organisation") company. As of November 2021, Minsktrans used 1,322 buses (plus 93 electric buses), 744 trolleybuses and 135 tramway cars in Minsk.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-76)^{#cite_ref-76}

The Minsk city government in 2003 decreed that local transport provision should be set at a minimum level of 1 vehicle (bus, trolleybus or tram) per 1,500 residents. The number of vehicles in use by Minsktrans is 2.2 times higher than the minimum level. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Public transport fares are controlled by the *city's executive committee* (city council). Single trip ticket for bus, trolleybus or tramway costs 0.75 [BYN](/wiki/BYR "BYR") (≈ USD 0.3),^[\[77\]](#cite_note-t.1-77)^ 0.80 BYN for metro and 0.90 BYN for express buses.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-t.1-77)^ Monthly ticket for one kind of transport costs 33 BYN and 61 [BYN](/wiki/New_Belarusian_ruble "New Belarusian ruble") for all five.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-t.1-77)^ Commercial [marshrutka](/wiki/Marshrutka "Marshrutka")'s prices varies from 1.5 to 2 BYN.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-t.1_77-2}  

### Rapid transit {#Rapid_transit}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Rapid transit")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/%D0%A1%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_1.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_1.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_1.jpg) [Vakzalnaja](/wiki/Vakza%C4%BAnaja_(Minsk_Metro) "Vakzaĺnaja (Minsk Metro)") station in the [Minsk Metro](/wiki/Minsk_Metro "Minsk Metro")  
Main article: [Minsk Metro](/wiki/Minsk_Metro "Minsk Metro")

Minsk is the only city in Belarus with an underground [metro](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") system. Construction of the metro began in 1977, soon after the city reached over a million people, and the first line with 8 stations was opened in 1984. Since then it has expanded into three lines: [Maskoŭskaja](/wiki/Masko%C5%ADskaja_Line "Maskoŭskaja Line"), [Aŭtazavodskaja](/wiki/A%C5%ADtazavodskaja_Line "Aŭtazavodskaja Line"), and [Zielienalužskaja](/wiki/Zelenaluzhskaya_Line "Zelenaluzhskaya Line") which are 19.1, 18.1 and 3.5 km (11.9, 11.2 and 2.2 mi) long with 15, 14 and 4 stations, respectively. On 7 November 2012, three new stations on the Moskovskaya Line were opened and another on 3 June 2014.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^. Construction of the third line began in 2011 and the first stage opened in 2020. Some layout plans speculate on a possible fourth line running from Vyasnyanka to Serabranka micro-rayons.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^
Stations of the new [Zielienalužskaja line](/wiki/Zelenaluzhskaya_Line "Zelenaluzhskaya Line") on video

Trains use 243 standard Russian metro-cars. On a typical day Minsk metro is used by 800,000 passengers. In 2007 ridership of Minsk metro was 262.1 million passengers,^[\[78\]](#cite_note-78)^ in 2017 ridership of Minsk metro was 284,1 million passengers,^[\[79\]](#cite_note-79)^ making it the 5th busiest metro network in the [former USSR](/wiki/Post-Soviet_states "Post-Soviet states") (behind Moscow, [St. Petersburg](/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg"), [Kyiv](/wiki/Kyiv "Kyiv") and [Kharkiv](/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv")). During peak hours trains run each 2--2.5 minutes. The metro network employs 3,435 staff.^[\[80\]](#cite_note-80)^{#cite_ref-80}

Most of the urban transport is being renovated to modern standards. For instance, all metro stations built since 2001 have passenger lifts from platform to street level, thus enabling the use of the newer stations by disabled passengers.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^^[\[81\]](#cite_note-81)^{#cite_ref-81}  

### Railway and intercity bus {#Railway_and_intercity_bus}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Railway and intercity bus")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Minsk-Central-Bus-Station.jpg/220px-Minsk-Central-Bus-Station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Minsk-Central-Bus-Station.jpg) Minsk Central Bus Station Nowadays [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Stadler_Astra_train%2C_Minsk_train_station%2C_Belarus%2C_pic._01.JPG/220px-Stadler_Astra_train%2C_Minsk_train_station%2C_Belarus%2C_pic._01.JPG)](/wiki/File:Stadler_Astra_train,_Minsk_train_station,_Belarus,_pic._01.JPG) Stadler FLIRT train (EPg), Minsk train station

Minsk is the largest transport hub in Belarus. Minsk is located at the junction of the [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw")-Moscow railway (built in 1871) running from the southwest to the northeast of the city and the [Liepaja](/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja "Liepāja")-[Romny](/wiki/Romny "Romny") railway (built in 1873) running from the northwest to the south. The first railway connects Russia with Poland and Germany; the second connects Ukraine with Lithuania and Latvia. They cross at the [Minsk-*Pasažyrski*](/wiki/Minsk_Passazhirsky_railway_station "Minsk Passazhirsky railway station") railway station, the main railway station of Minsk. The station was built in 1873 as Vilenski Vazkal. The initial wooden building was demolished in 1890 and rebuilt in stone. During World War II the Minsk railway station was completely destroyed. It was rebuilt in 1945 and 1946 and served until 1991. The new building of the Minsk-*Pasažyrski* railway station was built during 1991--2002. Its construction was delayed due to financial difficulties; now, however, Minsk boasts one of the most modern and up-to-date railway stations in the CIS. There were plans to move all [suburban rail](/wiki/Regional_rail "Regional rail") traffic from Minsk-*Pasažyrski* to the smaller stations, Minsk-*Uschodni* (East), Minsk-*Paŭdniovy* (South) and Minsk-*Paŭnočny* (North), by 2020. However, those plans were scrapped in favour of developing a more integrated system of suburban rail (branded as City Lines, operated by Belarusian Railways state enterprise). The system currently consists of 3 routes (to stations Bielaruś, Čyrvony Ściah, Rudziensk) all terminating at the central train station and is being served by 6 Stadler FLIRT train sets. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

There is an intercity bus station that links Minsk with the nearby airport, with the suburbs and other cities in Belarus and the neighboring countries. There are frequent services to Moscow, [Smolensk](/wiki/Smolensk "Smolensk"), [Vilnius](/wiki/Vilnius "Vilnius"), [Riga](/wiki/Riga "Riga") and [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

### Cycling {#Cycling}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Cycling")\]

According to the 2019 survey of 1934 people,^[\[82\]](#cite_note-82)^ Minsk had around 811,000 adult bicycles and 232,000 child and adolescent bicycles. In Minsk there is one bike for every 1.9 people. The total number of bicycles in Minsk exceeds the total number of cars (770,000 personal automobiles). 39% of Minsk residents have a personal bike. 43% of Minsk residents ride a bicycle once a month or more. As of 2017, the level of bicycle use is about 1% of all transport movements (for comparison: 12% in [Berlin](/wiki/Cycling_in_Berlin "Cycling in Berlin"), 50% in [Copenhagen](/wiki/Copenhagen "Copenhagen")).^[\[83\]](#cite_note-83)^{#cite_ref-83}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vieladaro%C5%BEka%2C_Minsk%2C_Belarus_-_panoramio_%2814%29.jpg/220px-Vieladaro%C5%BEka%2C_Minsk%2C_Belarus_-_panoramio_%2814%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Vieladaro%C5%BEka,_Minsk,_Belarus_-_panoramio_(14).jpg) Bike path in Minsk

Since 2015, an annual bicycle parade / bicycle carnival is held in Minsk, during which vehicles are blocked for several hours along Pobediteley (Peramohi) Avenue. The number of participants in 2019 was more than 20,000 and the number of registrations was about 12,000.^[\[84\]](#cite_note-84)^^[\[85\]](#cite_note-85)^^[\[86\]](#cite_note-86)^^[\[87\]](#cite_note-87)^ In 2017, the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union") funded the project "Urban cycling in Belarus" at a cost of €560,000, within the framework of which the public association Minsk Cycling Society together with the Council of Ministers created the regulatory document National Concept for the Development of Cycling in Belarus.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-88)^^[\[89\]](#cite_note-89)^ In 2020, Minsk entered the top 3 most cycling cities in the [CIS](/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States "Commonwealth of Independent States") -- after Moscow and [Saint Petersburg](/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg").^[\[90\]](#cite_note-90)^{#cite_ref-90}  

### Airports {#Airports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Airports")\]

[Minsk National Airport](/wiki/Minsk_National_Airport "Minsk National Airport") is located 42 km (26 mi) to the east of the city. It opened in 1982 and the current railway station opened in 1987. It is an [international airport](/wiki/International_airport "International airport") with flights to Europe and the Middle East.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-91)^{#cite_ref-91}

The former [Minsk-1 Airport](/wiki/Minsk-1_Airport "Minsk-1 Airport") closed in 2015.^[\[92\]](#cite_note-Russian_Aviation_Insider_2016_b473-92)^{#cite_ref-Russian_Aviation_Insider_2016_b473_92-0}

Minsk Borovaya Airfield (UMMB) is located in a suburb north-east of the city, next to Zaliony Luh Forest Park, housing Aero Club Minsk and Minsk Aviation Museum.^[\[93\]](#cite_note-93)^{#cite_ref-93}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Education")\]

Minsk has about 451 kindergartens, 241 schools, 22 further education colleges,^[\[94\]](#cite_note-94)^ and 29 higher education institutions,^[\[95\]](#cite_note-95)^ including 12 major national universities. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-95}  

### Major higher educational institutions {#Major_higher_educational_institutions}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Major higher educational institutions")\]

* [Academy of Public Administration under the aegis of the President of the Republic of Belarus](/wiki/Academy_of_Public_Administration_(Belarus) "Academy of Public Administration (Belarus)"). The Academy was established in 1991 and it acquired the status of a presidential institution in 1995. The Academy has 3 institutes: *Institute of Administrative Personnel* which has 3 departments, *Institute of Civil Service* which has 3 departments and *Research Institute of the Theory and Practice of [Public administration](/wiki/Public_administration "Public administration")*.
* [Belarusian State University](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University "Belarusian State University"). Major Belarusian universal university, founded in 1921. In 2006 had 15 major departments (Applied Mathematics and Informatics; Biology; Chemistry; Geography; Economics; [International relations](/wiki/International_relations "International relations"); Journalism; History; Humanitarian Sciences; Law; Mechanics and Mathematics; Philology; Philosophy and [Social sciences](/wiki/Social_sciences "Social sciences"); Physics; Radiophysics and Electronics). It also included 5 R\&D institutes, 24 Research Centres, 114 R\&D laboratories. The University employs over 2,400 lecturers and 1,000 research fellows; 1,900 of these hold PhD or Dr. Sc. degrees. There are 16,000 undergraduate students at the university, as well as over 700 PhD students. In 2018 [Olga Chupris](/wiki/Olga_Chupris "Olga Chupris") was the first female Vice-Rector appointed to the institution (Academic Work and Educational Innovations).
  * [Research Institute for Nuclear Problems of Belarusian State University](/wiki/Research_Institute_for_Nuclear_Problems_of_Belarusian_State_University "Research Institute for Nuclear Problems of Belarusian State University")
* [Belarusian State University of Agricultural Technology](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University_of_Agricultural_Technology "Belarusian State University of Agricultural Technology"). Specialised in [agricultural technology](/wiki/Agricultural_machinery "Agricultural machinery") and agricultural machinery.
* [Belarusian National Technical University](/wiki/Belarusian_National_Technical_University "Belarusian National Technical University"). Specialised in technical disciplines.
* [Belarusian State Medical University](/wiki/Belarusian_State_Medical_University "Belarusian State Medical University"). Specialised in Medicine and Dentistry. Since 1921 -- Medicine Department of the Belarusian State University. In 1930 becomes separate as *Belarusian Medical Institute*. In 2000 upgraded to university level. Has six departments.
* [Belarusian State Economic University](/wiki/Belarusian_State_Economic_University "Belarusian State Economic University"). Specialised in Finance and Economics. Founded in 1933 as *Belarusian Institute for National Economy*. Upgraded to university level in 1992.
* [Maxim Tank Belarusian State Pedagogical University](/wiki/Maxim_Tank_Belarusian_State_Pedagogical_University "Maxim Tank Belarusian State Pedagogical University"). Specialised in [teacher training](/wiki/Teacher_education "Teacher education") for secondary schools.
* [Belarusian State University of Informatics and Radioelectronics](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University_of_Informatics_and_Radioelectronics "Belarusian State University of Informatics and Radioelectronics"). Specialised in IT and radioelectronic technologies. Established in 1964 as *Minsk Institute for Radioelectronics*.
* [Belarusian State University of Physical Training](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University_of_Physical_Training "Belarusian State University of Physical Training"). Specialised in sports, coaches and PT teachers training.
* [Belarusian State Technological University](/wiki/Belarusian_State_Technological_University "Belarusian State Technological University"). Specialised in chemical and [pharmaceutical technology](/wiki/Pharmaceutics "Pharmaceutics"), in printing and forestry. Founded in 1930 as *Forestry Institute* in [Homel](/wiki/Gomel "Gomel"). In 1941 evacuated to Sverdlovsk, now [Yekaterinburg](/wiki/Yekaterinburg "Yekaterinburg"). Returned to Gomel in 1944, but in 1946 relocated to Minsk as *Belarusian Institute of Technology*. Upgraded to university level in 1993. Has nine departments.
* [Minsk State Linguistic University](/wiki/Minsk_State_Linguistic_University "Minsk State Linguistic University"). Specialised in [foreign languages](/wiki/Foreign_language "Foreign language"). Founded in 1948 as *Minsk Institute for Foreign Languages*. In 2006 had 8 departments. Major focus on English, French, German and Spanish.
* [Belarusian State University of Culture and Arts](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University_of_Culture_and_Arts "Belarusian State University of Culture and Arts"). Specializes in [cultural studies](/wiki/Cultural_studies "Cultural studies"), visual and Performing Arts. Founded in 1975 as *Minsk Institute of Culture*. Reorganized in 1993.
* [International Sakharov Environmental Institute](/wiki/International_Sakharov_Environmental_Institute "International Sakharov Environmental Institute"). Specialised in environmental sciences. Established in 1992 with the support from the United Nations. Focus on study and research of radio-ecological consequences of the [Chernobyl nuclear power station disaster](/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster "Chernobyl disaster") in 1986, which heavily affected Belarus.
* [Minsk Institute of Management](/wiki/Minsk_Institute_of_Management "Minsk Institute of Management"). The largest private higher educational institution in Belarus. Established in 1991. Specializes in Economics, Management, Marketing, Finance, [Psychology](/wiki/Psychology "Psychology") and Information technology.

  * [![Minsk State Linguistic University.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/MSLU_Minsk_2006.JPG/238px-MSLU_Minsk_2006.JPG)](/wiki/File:MSLU_Minsk_2006.JPG "Minsk State Linguistic University.")  
  [Minsk State Linguistic University](/wiki/Minsk_State_Linguistic_University "Minsk State Linguistic University").
  * [![Faculty of International Relations, Belarusian State University.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/%D0%A3%D0%BB.%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%83%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg/320px-%D0%A3%D0%BB.%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%83%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D0%BB.%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%83%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg "Faculty of International Relations, Belarusian State University.")  
  [Faculty of International Relations, Belarusian State University](/wiki/Faculty_of_International_Relations,_Belarusian_State_University "Faculty of International Relations, Belarusian State University").
  * [![Belarus State University rector's office.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Belarus-Minsk-BSU-Rector%27s_Office-2.jpg/241px-Belarus-Minsk-BSU-Rector%27s_Office-2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Belarus-Minsk-BSU-Rector%27s_Office-2.jpg "Belarus State University rector's office.")  
[Belarus State University](/wiki/Belarusian_State_University "Belarusian State University") rector's office.  

Honors {#Honors}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Honors")\]

A [minor planet](/wiki/Minor_planet "Minor planet") [3012 Minsk](/wiki/3012_Minsk "3012 Minsk") discovered by Soviet astronomer [Nikolai Chernykh](/wiki/Nikolai_Chernykh "Nikolai Chernykh") in 1979 is named after the city.^[\[96\]](#cite_note-96)^{#cite_ref-96}  

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Notable people")\]  
Main category: [People from Minsk](/wiki/Category:People_from_Minsk "Category:People from Minsk")

* [Andrei Pavlovich Ablameyko](/wiki/Andrei_Pavlovich_Ablameyko "Andrei Pavlovich Ablameyko") (born 1970), [Belarusian Greek Catholic](/wiki/Belarusian_Greek_Catholic_Church "Belarusian Greek Catholic Church") priest

* [Masha Bruskina](/wiki/Masha_Bruskina "Masha Bruskina") (1924--1941), World War II partisan
* [Siarhei Bulba](/wiki/Siarhei_Bulba "Siarhei Bulba") (born 1967), Belarusian politician, army officer and former leader of the paramilitary organisation White Legion
* [Veronika Cherkasova](/wiki/Veronika_Cherkasova "Veronika Cherkasova") (1959--2004), journalist^[\[99\]](#cite_note-99)^{#cite_ref-99}
* [Olga Chupris](/wiki/Olga_Chupris "Olga Chupris") (born 1969), first female Vice Rector of the Belarusian State University
* [Avraham Even-Shoshan](/wiki/Avraham_Even-Shoshan "Avraham Even-Shoshan") (1906--1984), Israeli linguist and lexicographer
* [Olga Fadeeva](/wiki/Olga_Fadeeva "Olga Fadeeva") (born 1978), actress
* [Sophie Fedorovitch](/wiki/Sophie_Fedorovitch "Sophie Fedorovitch") (1893--1953), ballet, opera and theatre designer, birthplace
* [Ella German](/wiki/Ella_German "Ella German") (born 1937), girlfriend of [Lee Harvey Oswald](/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald "Lee Harvey Oswald")
* [Moisei Ginzburg](/wiki/Moisei_Ginzburg "Moisei Ginzburg") (1892--1946), constructivist architect
* [Gennady Grushevoy](/wiki/Gennady_Grushevoy "Gennady Grushevoy") (1950--2014), academic, politician, human rights and environmental activist, winner of the 1999 Rafto Prize^[\[100\]](#cite_note-100)^{#cite_ref-100}
* [Alés Harun](/wiki/Al%C3%A9s_Harun "Alés Harun") (1887--1920), poet, writer and journalist^[\[101\]](#cite_note-101)^{#cite_ref-101}
* [Anatol Hrytskievich](/wiki/Anatol_Hrytskievich "Anatol Hrytskievich") (1929--2015), Belarusian historian^[\[102\]](#cite_note-102)^{#cite_ref-102}
* [Hienadź Karpienka](/wiki/Hienad%C5%BA_Karpienka "Hienadź Karpienka") (1949--1999), scientist and politician^[\[103\]](#cite_note-103)^{#cite_ref-103}
* [Uładzimir Katkoŭski](/wiki/U%C5%82adzimir_Katko%C5%ADski "Uładzimir Katkoŭski") (1976--2007), one of the founders of the Belarusian Wikipedia^[\[104\]](#cite_note-104)^{#cite_ref-104}
* [Jauhien Kulik](/wiki/Jauhien_Kulik "Jauhien Kulik") (1937--2002), artist and graphic designer who designed the 1991--95 coat of arms of Belarus, which was a version of the medieval symbol [Pahonia](/wiki/Pahonia "Pahonia")^[\[105\]](#cite_note-105)^{#cite_ref-105}
* [Pavel Latushka](/wiki/Pavel_Latushka "Pavel Latushka") (b.1973), Belarusian politician and opposition leader^[\[106\]](#cite_note-106)^^[\[107\]](#cite_note-107)^{#cite_ref-107}
* [Maryna Linchuk](/wiki/Maryna_Linchuk "Maryna Linchuk") (born 1987), fashion model
* [Ivan Lubennikov](/wiki/Ivan_Lubennikov "Ivan Lubennikov") (1951--2021), Russian painter, birthplace
* [Janka Lučyna](/wiki/Janka_Lu%C4%8Dyna "Janka Lučyna") (Jan Niesłuchowski) (1851--1897), poet^[\[108\]](#cite_note-108)^{#cite_ref-108}
* [Leanid Marakou](/wiki/Leanid_Marakou "Leanid Marakou") (1958--2016), journalist, writer^[\[109\]](#cite_note-109)^{#cite_ref-109}
* [Valery Marakoǔ](/wiki/Valery_Marakou "Valery Marakou") (1909--1937), Belarusian poet and translator, victim of [Stalin's purges](/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge")^[\[110\]](#cite_note-110)^{#cite_ref-110}
* [Yan Matusevich](/wiki/Yan_Matusevich "Yan Matusevich") (1946--1998) Catholic priest, and dean of the [Belarusian Greek Catholic Church](/wiki/Belarusian_Greek_Catholic_Church "Belarusian Greek Catholic Church")^[\[111\]](#cite_note-111)^{#cite_ref-111}
* [Louis B. Mayer](/wiki/Louis_B._Mayer "Louis B. Mayer") (1884--1957) American film producer, one of the founders of [Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer](/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer "Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer")
* [Bronislava Nijinska](/wiki/Bronislava_Nijinska "Bronislava Nijinska") (1890--1972), ballerina and choreographer of the Ballets Russes, birthplace
* [Lee Harvey Oswald](/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald "Lee Harvey Oswald") (1939--1963), assassin of US President [John F Kennedy](/wiki/John_F_Kennedy "John F Kennedy"), resided in Minsk from January 1960 to June 1962
* [Hillel Pewsner](/wiki/Hillel_Pewsner "Hillel Pewsner") (1922--2008), Chabad posek (legal scholar)^[\[112\]](#cite_note-112)^{#cite_ref-112}
* [Grigoriy Plaskov](/wiki/Grigoriy_Plaskov "Grigoriy Plaskov") (1898-1972), Soviet artillery lieutenant, birthplace
* [Alexander Rybak](/wiki/Alexander_Rybak "Alexander Rybak") (born 1986), winner of the [Eurovision Song Contest 2009](/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2009 "Eurovision Song Contest 2009") for Norway, birthplace
* [Uładzimier Samojła](/wiki/U%C5%82adzimier_Samoj%C5%82a "Uładzimier Samojła") (1878-1941), Belarusian critic, philosopher, journalist and a victim of Stalin's purges
* [Vitali Silitski](/wiki/Vitali_Silitski "Vitali Silitski") (1972--2011), political scientist, analyst, the first director of the Belarusian Institute for Strategic Studies^[\[113\]](#cite_note-113)^{#cite_ref-113}
* [Aliaksiej Skoblia](/wiki/Aliaksiej_Skoblia "Aliaksiej Skoblia") (nom de guerre Aliaksiej "Tur") (1990--2022), Belarusian fighter-volunteer of the [Kastuś Kalinoŭski Battalion](/wiki/Kastu%C5%9B_Kalino%C5%ADski_Battalion "Kastuś Kalinoŭski Battalion") posthumously awarded the title "Hero of Ukraine"^[\[114\]](#cite_note-114)^{#cite_ref-114}
* [Vanda Skuratovich](/wiki/Vanda_Skuratovich "Vanda Skuratovich") (1925--2010), Roman Catholic activist
* [Stanislav Shushkevich](/wiki/Stanislav_Shushkevich "Stanislav Shushkevich") (1934--2022), Belarusian politician and scientist, the first head of state of independent Belarus^[\[115\]](#cite_note-115)^^[\[116\]](#cite_note-116)^{#cite_ref-116}
* [Stefaniya Stanyuta](/wiki/Stefaniya_Stanyuta "Stefaniya Stanyuta") (1905--2000), theater and movie actress^[\[117\]](#cite_note-117)^{#cite_ref-117}
* [Alexander Taraikovsky](/wiki/Death_of_Alexander_Taraikovsky "Death of Alexander Taraikovsky") (1986--2020), entrepreneur killed during the protests against the [2020 Belarusian presidential election](/wiki/2020_Belarusian_presidential_election "2020 Belarusian presidential election")^[\[118\]](#cite_note-118)^{#cite_ref-118}
* [Barys Tasman](/wiki/Barys_Tasman "Barys Tasman") (1954--2022), journalist, sports writer
* [George Tsisetski](/wiki/George_Tsisetski "George Tsisetski") (b. 1985), film director, screenwriter, dramatist and visual artist
* [Rachel Wischnitzer](/wiki/Rachel_Wischnitzer "Rachel Wischnitzer") (1885--1989), architect and art historian
* [Jazep Jucho](/wiki/Jazep_Jucho "Jazep Jucho") (1921--2004), lawyer, historian and writer and a leading Belarusian authority on the [laws of the Grand Duchy of Lithuania](/wiki/Statutes_of_Lithuania "Statutes of Lithuania")^[\[119\]](#cite_note-119)^{#cite_ref-119}
* [Simcha Zorin](/wiki/Simcha_Zorin "Simcha Zorin") (1902--1974) World War II partisan
* [Asher ben Löb Günzburg](/wiki/Asher_ben_L%C3%B6b_G%C3%BCnzburg "Asher ben Löb Günzburg") (1754--1823), rabbi

### Musicians {#Musicians}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Musicians")\]

* [Angelica Agurbash](/wiki/Angelica_Agurbash "Angelica Agurbash") (born 1970), Belarusian singer, Eurovision participant^[\[120\]](#cite_note-120)^{#cite_ref-120}
* [Marina Gordon](/wiki/Marina_Gordon "Marina Gordon") (1917--2013) soprano, birthplace^[\[121\]](#cite_note-121)^{#cite_ref-121}
* [Irma Jaunzem](/wiki/Irma_Jaunzem "Irma Jaunzem") (1897--1975), mezzo-soprano singer and folk song specialist
* [Boris Khaykin](/wiki/Boris_Khaykin "Boris Khaykin") (1904--1978), conductor
* [Yung Lean](/wiki/Yung_Lean "Yung Lean") (born 1996), Swedish rapper \& musician, birthplace
* [Źmicier Sidarovič](/wiki/%C5%B9micier_Sidarovi%C4%8D "Źmicier Sidarovič") (1965--2014), musician^[\[122\]](#cite_note-122)^{#cite_ref-122}
* [Lavon Volski](/wiki/Lavon_Volski "Lavon Volski") (b. 1965), musician^[\[123\]](#cite_note-123)^{#cite_ref-123}

### Sport {#Sport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Sport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raskina10-syd20000929blr-450ver2.jpg/180px-Raskina10-syd20000929blr-450ver2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Raskina10-syd20000929blr-450ver2.jpg) [Yulia Raskina](/wiki/Yulia_Raskina "Yulia Raskina") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/2022-12-22_ALBA_Berlin_gegen_Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_B.C._%28EuroLeague_2022-23%29_by_Sandro_Halank%E2%80%93066.jpg/180px-2022-12-22_ALBA_Berlin_gegen_Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_B.C._%28EuroLeague_2022-23%29_by_Sandro_Halank%E2%80%93066.jpg)](/wiki/File:2022-12-22_ALBA_Berlin_gegen_Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_B.C._(EuroLeague_2022-23)_by_Sandro_Halank%E2%80%93066.jpg) [Roman Sorkin](/wiki/Roman_Sorkin "Roman Sorkin")

* [Andrei Arlovski](/wiki/Andrei_Arlovski "Andrei Arlovski") (born 1979), grew up and lived in Minsk before moving to the US to fight in the Ultimate Fighting Championship
* [Victoria Azarenka](/wiki/Victoria_Azarenka "Victoria Azarenka") (born 1989), former World No. 1 tennis player and 2012 and 2013 Australian Open winner, born in Minsk moving to [Arizona](/wiki/Arizona "Arizona") at 16
* [Yuri Bessmertny](/wiki/Yuri_Bessmertny "Yuri Bessmertny") (born 1987), kickboxer
* [Svetlana Boginskaya](/wiki/Svetlana_Boginskaya "Svetlana Boginskaya") (born 1973), gold medal-winning gymnast at the 1988 and [1992 Olympics](/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics "1992 Summer Olympics"), birthplace
* [Isaac Boleslavsky](/wiki/Isaac_Boleslavsky "Isaac Boleslavsky") (1919-1977), chess grandmaster
* [Darya Domracheva](/wiki/Darya_Domracheva "Darya Domracheva") (born 1986), gold (4 times) and bronze medal-winning biathlete at the 2010 and [2014 Winter Olympics](/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics "2014 Winter Olympics")
* [Boris Gelfand](/wiki/Boris_Gelfand "Boris Gelfand") (born 1968), Israeli chess Grandmaster
* [Max Geller](/wiki/Max_Geller_(Wrestler) "Max Geller (Wrestler)") (born 1971), Israeli Olympic wrestler
* [Alexei Ignashov](/wiki/Alexei_Ignashov "Alexei Ignashov") (born 1978), kickboxer, multiple Muay Thai and K-1 world champion
* [Oleg Karavayev](/wiki/Oleg_Karavayev "Oleg Karavayev") (1936-1978), wrestler and Olympic champion
* [Viktar Kuprejčyk](/wiki/Viktor_Kupreichik "Viktor Kupreichik") (1949--2017), chess grandmaster^[\[124\]](#cite_note-124)^{#cite_ref-124}
* [Isaak Mazel](/wiki/Isaak_Mazel "Isaak Mazel") (1911-1945), chess master
* [Max Mirnyi](/wiki/Max_Mirnyi "Max Mirnyi") (born 1977), tennis player
* [Aleksey Orlovich](/wiki/Aleksey_Orlovich "Aleksey Orlovich") (born 2002), Belarusian professional footballer
* [Artsiom Parakhouski](/wiki/Artsiom_Parakhouski "Artsiom Parakhouski") (born 1987), basketball player
* [Yulia Raskina](/wiki/Yulia_Raskina "Yulia Raskina") (born 1982), individual rhythmic gymnast, won the All-Around Silver at the 2000 Sydney Olympics
* [Roman Rubinshteyn](/wiki/Roman_Rubinshteyn "Roman Rubinshteyn") (born 1996), Belarusian-Israeli basketball player in the [Israeli Basketball Premier League](/wiki/Israeli_Basketball_Premier_League "Israeli Basketball Premier League")
* [Aryna Sabalenka](/wiki/Aryna_Sabalenka "Aryna Sabalenka") (born 1998), [2023 Australian Open](/wiki/2023_Australian_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_singles "2023 Australian Open – Women's singles") winner and former [world No. 1 tennis player](/wiki/List_of_WTA_number_1_ranked_singles_tennis_players "List of WTA number 1 ranked singles tennis players"), born in Minsk moving to [Miami](/wiki/Miami "Miami") at 23
* [Yegor Sharangovich](/wiki/Yegor_Sharangovich "Yegor Sharangovich") (born 1998), ice hockey player
* [Yuri Shulman](/wiki/Yuri_Shulman "Yuri Shulman") (born 1975), Belarusian-American chess grandmaster
* [Mark Slavin](/wiki/Mark_Slavin "Mark Slavin") (1954-1972), Israeli Olympic Greco-Roman wrestler and victim of the [Munich massacre](/wiki/Munich_massacre "Munich massacre") at the 1972 Summer Olympics
* [Anna Smashnova](/wiki/Anna_Smashnova "Anna Smashnova") (born 1976), Belarusian-born Israeli tennis player
* [Roman Sorkin](/wiki/Roman_Sorkin "Roman Sorkin") (born 1996), Belarusian-born Israeli basketball player in the [Israeli Basketball Premier League](/wiki/Israeli_Basketball_Premier_League "Israeli Basketball Premier League")
* [Diana Vaisman](/wiki/Diana_Vaisman "Diana Vaisman") (born 1998), Belarusian-born Israeli sprinter

Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}
-----------------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Minsk&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]  
See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Belarus](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Belarus "List of twin towns and sister cities in Belarus")

Minsk is [twinned](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") with:^[\[125\]](#cite_note-125)^{#cite_ref-125}  
* [Abu Dhabi](/wiki/Abu_Dhabi "Abu Dhabi"), United Arab Emirates (2007)
* [Ankara](/wiki/Ankara "Ankara"), Turkey (2007)
* [Bangalore](/wiki/Bangalore "Bangalore"), India (1986)
* [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), China (2016)
* [Bishkek](/wiki/Bishkek "Bishkek"), Kyrgyzstan (1997)
* [Bonn](/wiki/Bonn "Bonn"), Germany (1993)
* [Changchun](/wiki/Changchun "Changchun"), China (1992)
* [Chişinău](/wiki/Chi%C5%9Fin%C4%83u "Chişinău"), Moldova (2000)
* [Detroit](/wiki/Detroit "Detroit"), United States (1979)^[\[126\]](#cite_note-126)^{#cite_ref-126}
* [Dushanbe](/wiki/Dushanbe "Dushanbe"), Tajikistan (1998)
* [Eindhoven](/wiki/Eindhoven "Eindhoven"), Netherlands (1994)
* [Gaziantep](/wiki/Gaziantep "Gaziantep"), Turkey (2018)
* [Hanoi](/wiki/Hanoi "Hanoi"), Vietnam (2004)
* [Havana](/wiki/Havana "Havana"), Cuba (2005)
* [Ho Chi Minh City](/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City "Ho Chi Minh City"), Vietnam (2008)
* [Islamabad](/wiki/Islamabad "Islamabad"), Pakistan (2015)
* [Kaluga](/wiki/Kaluga "Kaluga"), Russia (2015)
* [Murmansk](/wiki/Murmansk "Murmansk"), Russia (2014)
* [Nizhny Novgorod](/wiki/Nizhny_Novgorod "Nizhny Novgorod"), Russia (2017)
* [Novosibirsk](/wiki/Novosibirsk "Novosibirsk"), Russia (2012)
* [Rostov-on-Don](/wiki/Rostov-on-Don "Rostov-on-Don"), Russia (2018)
* [Sendai](/wiki/Sendai "Sendai"), Japan (1973)
* [Shanghai](/wiki/Shanghai "Shanghai"), China (2019)
* [Shenzhen](/wiki/Shenzhen "Shenzhen"), China (2014)
* [Tbilisi](/wiki/Tbilisi "Tbilisi"), Georgia (2015)
* [Tehran](/wiki/Tehran "Tehran"), Iran (2006)
* [Ufa](/wiki/Ufa "Ufa"), Russia (2017)
* [Ulyanovsk](/wiki/Ulyanovsk "Ulyanovsk"), Russia (2015)
